§ 151.01 PURPOSE AND INTENT; APPLICABILITY.
   (A)   The purpose and intent of this chapter is to establish and provide
minimum acceptable standards, requirements and regulations for the planned use,
development and maintenance of mobile homes within the corporate limits of the
town, to include both free-standing mobile homes and those located in mobile
home parks, in the interest of the health, safety and general welfare of the
residents.
   (B)   Except as hereinafter provided, no mobile home shall be used or
maintained, and no mobile home park or mobile home site shall be used,
maintained or developed except in conformance with the standards of this
chapter.
(Prior Code, § 12-301) (Ord. 2022-003, passed 7-12-2022)
§ 151.02 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CODE ENFORCEMENT OFFICIAL. The officer or other designated authority charged
with the administration and enforcement of this code.
   DEVELOPER. Any person engaged in the development or planning of a mobile
home park.
   DWELLING. Any structure or vehicle occupied or used primarily for a
residential premises which may or may not contain sleeping, bath, toilet,
cooking and refrigeration facilities.
   EXPANSION OF A MOBILE HOME PARK. Increasing either the total land area or
the total number of mobile homes or mobile home spaces or lots in a park.
   FREE-STANDING MOBILE HOME. Any mobile home not located in a mobile home park
or mobile home subdivision.
   MOBILE HOME. A manufactured, detached structure which is originally
designed, constructed and used for long-term occupancy as a complete single-
family dwelling, is mounted on a permanent chassis with wheels attached
thereto, and which is transportable in one or more sections at least eight feet
in width and 28 feet in length.
   MOBILE HOME PARK. Land or property that is used or intended to be used or
rented for occupancy by mobile homes, including all necessary utilities,
streets and other common amenities.
   MOBILE HOME PARK SITE PLAN. A scale drawing prepared by a registered
architect, landscape architect, engineer or land surveyor which meets the
requirements of §
151.06(B) for a mobile home park.
   MOBILE HOME PERMIT. A permit issued by the town for construction and/or
operation of a mobile home park or a mobile home site.
   MOBILE HOME SITE. A plat, lot or tract of land designed to accommodate a
free-standing mobile home.
   MOBILE HOME SPACE. A plat, lot or tract of land within a mobile home park
designed to accommodate one mobile home.
   MODULAR STRUCTURE. A transportable, non-vehicular, prefabricated structure,
requiring an independent foundation, which is designed and constructed for
movement from a point of fabrication to a permanent erection or location site.
    PERMITTEE. Any person to whom a permit has been issued within the scope of
this chapter.
   PERSON. Any individual, partnership, trust, association, corporation or
combination thereof.
   RECREATIONAL VEHICLE. A vehicular type unit designed primarily for temporary
living quarters for recreational, camping or travel use, which either has its
own motive power or is mounted on or towed by another vehicle and has its own
potable water storage tank and waste storage tank. For the purposes of this
chapter. RECREATIONAL VEHICLES shall be considered a mobile home when occupied
more than 90% of the time for 30 or more consecutive days.
   STRUCTURAL ADDITION. Any roofed, canopied or enclosed porch, room or
structure used in connection with a mobile home.
(Prior Code, § 12-302) (Ord. 2022-003, passed 7-12-2022)
§ 151.03 MOBILE HOME OCCUPANCY PERMIT.
   No occupancy permits for any mobile or manufactured home, whether free-
standing or located in a mobile home park and located within the town after the
date of this chapter unless such mobile or manufactured home shall meet all the
following safety and health requirements.
   (A)   The mobile or manufactured home shall meet and conform to the
standards of 63 O.S. § 1084, or any successor statute as well as any federal
standards related to mobile or manufactured home construction safety.
   (B)   The mobile home shall be less than five years old or a variance
approved by the Town Board.
   (C)   Tie down anchors shall be securely installed in soil providing a
stable foundation for the mobile home.
   (D)   (1)   It shall be the responsibility of the owner or occupant of any
mobile home, within a period of no longer than 30 days after moving such mobile
home onto an approved site, to cause such mobile home to be totally skirted of
metal or other non-degradable solid material.
      (2)   The skirting shall be secured to the mobile home and to the ground
in a manner that will prevent the intrusion of animals and will reduce the
hazards of strong winds under said home.
   (E)   The town reserves the right to request that home be inspected if any
of the items in this section are questionable to any representative of the
town.
(Ord. 2022-003, passed 7-12-2022)
§ 151.04 USE, OCCUPANCY AND LOCATION OF MOBILE HOMES AND MODULAR STRUCTURES.
   The use, occupancy and location of mobile homes and modular structures are
governed by the provisions of this chapter and the code of ordinances of the
town.
(Prior Code, § 12-303)
§ 151.05 TEMPORARY NONRESIDENTIAL USE OF MOBILE HOMES AND MODULAR STRUCTURES.
   (A)   Temporary permit required; requirements for issuance established.
      (1)   Any person who desires to use a mobile home or a modular structure
on a temporary basis for a field or local branch office, for demonstration or
for a charitable and nonprofit purpose may do so upon issuance of a temporary
mobile home permit by the Town Clerk-Treasurer. The prospective user shall
apply for such permit by filing a written application with the Code Enforcement
Official, accompanied by a non-refundable application fee of $100, payable to
the town. Such application shall include the exact location where the mobile
home or modular structure will be placed, a full explanation and description of
the use or activity which will be conducted within the mobile home or modular
structure, and a statement specifying the period of time for which such
temporary use will be required.
      (2)   Upon a finding by the Code Enforcement Official that the proposed
use is permitted by this section, that such use will not exceed 12 months in
duration and upon the applicant’s posting a cash or surety removal bond as
hereinafter required, the official shall issue a temporary mobile home permit
for any requested period of time not exceeding 12 months.
   (B)   Removal bond. Prior to the issuance of a temporary mobile home permit,
the applicant shall post with the Town Clerk-Treasurer a cash or surety bond in
the amount of $500 to defray removal costs in the event the applicant fails to
remove the mobile home or modular structure at the expiration of the temporary
mobile home permit.
   (C)   Permit for extended use.
      (1)   The use of any property as a temporary location site for a mobile
home or modular structure in excess of 12 months shall not be considered to be
a temporary use within the meaning of this section, and no additional temporary
permits shall be issued by the Code Enforcement Official; provided, however,
that permits for extended temporary use beyond the initial 12 months may be
obtained by the following persons:
         (a)   Building contractors involved with an ongoing construction
project on the same property on which such mobile home or modular structure is
located; and
         (b)   Public schools (as defined in 70 O.S. § 1-106) using such mobile
home or modular structure as temporary classrooms.
      (2)   The Code Enforcement Official shall either issue the requested
permit for extended use or deny the application in writing, giving the reasons
for such denial, within ten working days after the filing of such application.
No extended use permit shall be issued for a period of time exceeding 12
months. Extended use permits may be re-issued by the Code Enforcement Official
upon the expiration of an existing extended use permit.
   (D)   Limitations upon occupancy of temporarily located mobile homes and
modular structures. Holders of temporary permits and their employees may occupy
a mobile home or a modular structure on a 24-hour basis, provided that:
      (1)   Such occupancy is accessory and subordinate to a principal
nonresidential use of the property upon which such mobile home or modular
structure is located; and
      (2)   Such 24-hour occupancy does not thereby establish a dwelling unit
within the meaning of the zoning code of the town and 42 O.S. unless otherwise
permitted by a zoning variance granted by the Town Board of Adjustment.
(Prior Code, § 12-304)
§ 151.06 GENERAL REQUIREMENTS FOR MOBILE HOME PARKS.
   (A)   (1)   Utility connections. Electrical, mechanical and plumbing
connections, where required, shall comply with the respective codes of the
town.
      (2)   Fire hydrants.
         (a)   Where existing fire hydrants are farther than 1,000 feet from
the most distant mobile home or recreational vehicle space, additional fire
hydrants shall be provided and located as required by the Fire Chief of the
town.
         (b)   The Fire Chief shall approve or deny submitted plans within
seven days after receipt thereof.
      (3)   Street lighting. Streetlamps shall be positioned no less than every
200 feet throughout the park. Such lamps shall be 20 feet above ground level
and shall contain bulbs of at least 100 watts. All lamps shall be shaded and
positioned so as to avoid glare on adjoining properties.
(Prior Code, § 12-305)
   (B)   The following general provisions shall apply to mobile home parks.
      (1)   Every person desiring to create, establish, expand, develop or
construct a mobile home park shall submit a site plan application on the forms
supplied by the town. Such application shall include the following:
         (a)   A legal description of the site;
         (b)   A filing fee of $200; and
         (c)   A site plan which shall include the following on a scaled
drawing of appropriate dimensions:
            1.   Written legal description of the site, including the size of
the property in acres, or a fraction, thereof;
            2.   Approval by a registered engineer, architect, landscape
surveyor licensed in the state, so indicated by signature and seal;
            3.   A north arrow, date, scale and appropriate legend;
            4.   Two-foot contour intervals;
            5.   Location and size of all easements, utilities and rights-of-
way existing and proposed;
            6.   All public and private streets, including paving type;
            7.   Location and size of all existing and proposed structures,
including mobile home spaces;
            8.   Location and size of open space or common areas;
            9.   Location and type of landscaping and ground cover;
            10.   Location and type of material and in fences and other
screening;
            11.   Language with signature blocks to indicate the approval of
the owners of the land and the town for recording purposes; and
            12.   A scale drawing of appropriate dimension of a typical mobile
home space which shows the location and size of all existing permanent
improvements, including pads, off-street parking with surface types, utility
connections and all front, side and rear yard setback distances.
      (2)   The town may require certain alterations, modifications or
amendments of the mobile home park site plan when deemed necessary for the
inclusion of easements, rights-of-way and utilities and the like. Improvement
bonds may also be required for public utilities on the subject property for
fire hydrants, water lines, sewer lines, drainage structures and other similar
projects.
      (3)   The site plan shall be reviewed by the Town Board of Trustees for
compliance with this chapter and other relevant provisions of this code.
      (4)   The town shall approve, approve conditionally or return for further
study or disapprove the site plan. Approval of the site plan shall be
documented by the signatures of the presiding officers of the town, and
acceptance by signature of the owner(s) on the certificate located on the
original of the site plan. A reproducible copy of the site plan with all
required signatures shall be furnished to the town at the applicant’s expense.
      (5)   Occupancy permits for the mobile home park will be issued only
after inspection by the town and only if the mobile home park has been
developed in accordance with the provisions of this chapter and the approved
site plan.
      (6)   (a)   It shall be the responsibility of every person owning a
mobile home park to maintain a current register of the names of all mobile home
owners within such mobile home park and the date every mobile home was brought
within such mobile home park.
         (b)   For reasonable cause, such register shall be available during
normal working hours for inspection by the town.
      (7)   A mobile home shall not be allowed, permitted or authorized in any
street or public right-of-way.
(Prior Code, § 12-309)
§ 151.07 LOCATION REQUIREMENTS.
   A mobile home for living or sleeping purposes shall only be located, used,
kept and maintained within a mobile home park as duly permitted and provided
for in this chapter; provided, that a free-standing mobile home may be located
on a mobile home site that is in compliance with this code.
(Prior Code, § 12-306)
§ 151.08 FREE-STANDING MOBILE HOME SITES.
   (A)   General provisions. The following general provisions shall apply to
free-standing mobile homes.
      (1)   Every person desiring to create, establish, expand, develop or
construct a mobile home site shall submit a site plan which includes the
following:
         (a)   A legal description of the property; and
         (b)   A scaled drawing of appropriate dimensions which includes the
following:
            1.   Written legal description of the site, including the size of
the site in square feet or in acres;
            2.   Location of the site on the property;
            3.   Location and size of existing and other proposed structures on
the property;
            4.   Location and size of all easements, utilities and rights-of-
way, existing and proposed; and
            5.   A north arrow, date, scale and appropriate legend.
      (2)   Each mobile home site shall satisfy all of the following
requirements:
         (a)   It shall have an all-weather surfaced entry area, consisting of
gravel, asphalt or concrete;
         (b)   It shall have at least two all-weather (consisting of gravel,
asphalt or concrete) off-street parking spaces together measuring no less than
18 feet wide and 20 feet long;
         (c)   The mobile home shall be not less than 20 feet from any other
mobile home or permanent building, including any structural additions thereto;
         (d)   The mobile home shall be not less than the setback distance of
25 feet from the front yard, and 15 feet for the rear and any exterior property
line, easement or right-of-way, and ten feet from the side yard lines;
         (e)   Connections to utilities shall adhere to the provisions
contained in §
151.12; and
         (f)   The site shall be arranged so that it abuts on a driveway or
street of at least 16 feet in width, giving access directly from a public
street. All driveways and roads shall be graded so as to have natural drainage
and shall be well lit at night and unobstructed.
   (B)   Any mobile home site permitted, allowed and authorized within the
corporate limits of the town prior to the effective date of this chapter and in
compliance with any laws hereby repealed or amended, may continue to be
maintained under the laws then in effect; provided, however, that all mobile
homes whether or not previously existing shall be maintained in compliance with
the provisions of this chapter.
   (C)   A mobile home site permitted hereunder shall be deemed abandoned if
not used for a period of six months after the effective date of this chapter
and shall thereafter be required to comply with all of its provisions.
   (D)   Any person seeking to expand any mobile home site shall comply with
all the provisions of this chapter as they affect and pertain to that portion
of such mobile home site, or that tract of land, sought to be expanded upon.
(Prior Code, § 12-307)
§ 151.09 MOBILE HOME PARK LICENSES REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to establish, operate or maintain or
permit to be established, operated or maintained upon any property controlled
or owned by him or her, a mobile homes park, as defined in this chapter,
without having first secured a license therefor and having paid the filing fee
for inspection of the construction of such park.
(Prior Code, § 12-308) Penalty, see §
151.99
§ 151.10 DEVELOPMENT STANDARDS.
   Development of mobile home parks shall be in accordance with the following
standards.
   (A)   Dimensional and site development requirements. The minimum lot size
for a mobile home park shall be 90,000 contiguous square feet. Open space,
streets and drainage of the mobile home park shall meet the requirements stated
below.
      (1)   No less than 10% nor more than one acre of a mobile home park
exclusive of easements, rights-of-way, setbacks or shelters shall be required
to be designated, preserved and set apart for common facilities open space and
recreation. Where possible, this open space or recreation area should be
consolidated to provide a meaningful recreation area.
      (2)   (a)   A convenient circulation system for vehicular movement shall
be provided within a mobile home park by means of minor streets and properly
located collector streets. Collector streets shall be hard surfaced for a
minimum width of 29 feet. All other streets and drives shall be hard surfaced
for a minimum width of 20 feet.
         (b)   Private streets and drives may provide parallel parking on one
side provided an additional eight feet of width is hard surfaced.
         (c)   Private streets and drives may be one-way only when less than
500 feet long, serving less than 25 mobile home spaces, and a minimum of 16
feet wide; and
         (d)   Dead-end streets shall have a cul-de-sac with a diameter of no
less than 80 feet.
      (3)   The drainage system of all lots shall be designed in accordance
with all relevant provisions of this code to minimize the possibilities of soil
erosion, sedimentation and increased runoff which might cause flooding of
downstream properties. Adequate easements shall be provided to protect drainage
ways from encroachment, and to protect property from drainage by periodic
flooding. Excavation of topographic area having a grade of more than 10% shall
be prohibited unless it is determined that adequate provisions to control
erosion that may result from such excavation are guaranteed. Alternatives to
sodding or seeding may be considered when said alternative method is intended
to accomplish the limiting of dust, erosion and sedimentation of drainage
areas.
   (B)   Individual lot requirements. Each mobile home space shall satisfy all
of the following requirements.
      (1)   It shall have a hard surfaced entry area.
      (2)   It shall have two hard surfaced off-street parking spaces no less
than 18 feet in width by 20 feet.
      (3)   It shall have a visible identifying number.
      (4)   It shall provide setbacks as set forth in §
151.12.
      (5)   No mobile home, mobile home addition, storage building or related
structure or appurtenance shall be located, constructed or maintained within
any street, dedicated easement, right-of-way or drainage area.
   (C)   Sanitation. A mobile home that does not have a built-in bathroom with
water closet, lavatory and shower or tub in working condition shall not be
maintained, authorized, permitted nor occupied in a mobile home park.
   (D)   Utilities. Utility service shall be provided in a safe and reliable
manner in accordance with the following specifications.
      (1)   All plumbing and electrical systems, connections, installations,
fixtures and equipment shall be installed and maintained in full compliance
with those applicable provisions of this section and this code.
      (2)   (a)   An adequate supply of safe water of satisfactory quality
under sufficient pressure shall be provided to and for all mobile homes and
utility buildings. Water connections shall be made to the town’s water
distribution system where feasible, and when not feasible, to a water system
that is maintained in accordance with the standards, regulations and laws of
the state relating thereto.
         (b)   Adequate fire hydrant facilities with the required fire flow
shall be specified and approved by the town for each mobile home park.
      (3)   An approved sewer disposal system, being adequate and safe, shall
be provided for each mobile home and community structure having plumbing
fixtures therein. A sewer connection shall be made to the town’s sanitary sewer
where feasible, and where not feasible, to a sewer system that is constructed
or maintained in accordance with the standards, regulations and laws of the
state relating thereto.
      (4)   The design of the electrical system shall meet the criteria of the
utility company furnishing service.
      (5)   All interior private streets, drives and pedestrians’ walkways
within a mobile home park shall be lighted at night with light equivalent to 60
watts at intervals of 200 feet.
      (6)   Methods and facilities for the collection, storage, handling and
disposal of garbage and refuse shall be provided for as determined and in
accordance with this code.
   (E)   Community fuel supply and storage. The installation, use and storage
of gas shall be in accordance with the following requirements.
      (1)   A gas piping system, if installed, and maintained in accordance
with all pertinent provisions of this section, the town’s fire prevention code,
and the laws of the state relating to plumbing, so as to provide a supply of
gas sufficient to meet the maximum demand without undue loss of pressure at the
connection point to the mobile home furthest from the source of supply. All gas
piping shall be installed by a licensed contractor only.
      (2)   The gas supply shall be connected in the proper manner, ensuring
that the piping is properly purged and free from leaks and that all appliances
are suitable for the supply.
      (3)   Before a mobile home is moved, adequate arrangements shall be made
to assure that all gas connections are properly disconnected.
      (4)   If liquefied petroleum gas is to be used, its installation and
storage shall be in strict compliance with all applicable provisions of this
code and the statutes of the state.
   (F)   Service, administrative and other buildings. Buildings maintained and
intended for uses other than a dwelling shall meet the following requirements.
      (1)   One mobile home may be used as an administrative office. Other
administrative offices and service buildings for housing sanitation, laundry or
other facilities shall be of permanent structure, complying with all pertinent
provisions of this code relating to construction and maintenance, for the use
of all park residents.
      (2)   All service buildings shall be adequately lighted at all times,
well-ventilated with screen openings and constructed of such moisture proof
materiel, including painted woodwork to permit repeated cleaning and washing,
and shall be provided with space heating equipment adequate to maintain 68°F in
temperature at outside design conditions.
      (3)   All service buildings and grounds of a mobile home park shall be
maintained in a clean and sightly condition, free from any condition that will
menace the health of any mobile home park resident therein or otherwise
constitute a nuisance.
   (G)   Fire protection. No tow car or mobile home shall be parked, placed or
allowed to remain at any time on a public or private street, or pedestrian
walkway within a mobile home park. Fire hydrants located no greater than 600
feet apart as measured by street travel requiring the inspection and approval
of the Fire Chief, and water mains, both of adequate size and number, shall be
provided for the protection of the mobile home park.
(Prior Code, § 12-310)
§ 151.11 MOBILE HOME TIE DOWNS AND SKIRTING.
   (A)   Tie downs. It shall be the responsibility of the owner or occupant of
any mobile home to cause such mobile home to be anchored and tied down securely
in accordance with the following minimal standards within a period of no longer
than 30 days after moving a mobile home into a mobile home park.
      (1)   A mobile home with integrated or integral tie down attachments
shall be utilized in accordance with the mobile home manufacturers installation
procedures.
      (2)   Mobile homes without integrated or integral tie down attachments
shall utilize over the home tie downs as follows: A mobile home shall have two
over the home ties, each to be as close to each end of said home as possible
with the straps at the stud and rafter points.
      (3)   In addition to the over-the-home straps, a mobile home greater than
50 feet but less than or equal to 70 feet in length shall have two frame ties
at the center of said home, and a mobile home greater than 70 feet in length
shall have four frame ties spaced along the center of said home.
      (4)   Double-wide mobile homes need not be provided with over-the-home
ties. Frame ties shall be provided with at least four required for double-wide
mobile homes less than 50 feet in length; at least six required for double-wide
mobile homes greater than 50 feet but less than or equal to 70 feet in length;
and at least eight required for mobile homes greater than 70 feet in length.
      (5)   Tie down anchors shall be securely installed in soil providing a
stable foundation to withstand a minimum pull of 3,750 pounds for each ten feet
of a mobile home.
      (6)   All ties and connectors shall be of a type approved by the United
States Department of Housing and Urban Development (H.U.D.) for mobile home
anchoring.
      (7)   All piers shall be of standard concrete block construction, eight
by 16 inches, spaced at no more than ten-foot intervals and no further than
five feet from the ends of a mobile home. Piers shall rest on solid concrete
blocks or pads of concrete measuring no less than eight by 16 by four inches
forming a base 16 inches square. For leveling purposes, wood blocking no less
than the nominal dimensions of eight by 16 inches with a maximum thickness of
four inches can be used.
   (B)   Skirting. It shall be the responsibility of the owner or occupant of
any mobile home, within a period of no longer than 30 days after moving such
mobile home into a mobile home park, to cause such mobile home to be totally
skirted of metal or other non-degradable solid material. The skirting shall be
secured to the mobile home and to the ground in a manner that will prevent the
intrusion of animals and will reduce the hazards of strong winds under said
home.
(Prior Code, § 12-311)
§ 151.12 CODES APPLICABLE.
   (A)   All plumbing, electrical, building and other work on any park licensed
under this chapter shall be performed in accordance with the ordinances of the
town regulating the same unless said ordinances are specifically made
inapplicable under the terms thereof or under the terms of this chapter; only a
person who is properly licensed under the provisions of this code may connect
and disconnect water, gas and sewage facilities to mobile homes located in any
park and any free-standing mobile home site.
   (B)   Sewer connection inspection fees for mobile home parks shall be those
applicable to family dwellings, and each site within the park shall be deemed a
family living unit.
(Prior Code, § 12-312)
§ 151.13 OTHER REGULATIONS APPLICABLE.
   All ordinances enacted by the town pertaining to traffic and vehicles, the
control of pets and/or animals, shall be fully as effective within the park as
though streets and driveways were dedicated to public use, and the consent and
agreement of the owner of said park, streets and highways thereto shall be a
condition precedent to the issuance of said license.
(Prior Code, § 12-313)
§ 151.14 PERMIT REQUIRED.
   (A)   Permit required to move mobile home. It is unlawful for any person to
move any mobile home or modular home along or across any street or public way
within the corporate limits of the town without a permit from the Town Clerk-
Treasurer; provided, that nothing contained herein shall apply to the moving of
mobile homes through the town strictly on any state or federal highway.
   (B)   Permit required to locale mobile home within corporate limits.
      (1)   It shall be unlawful to locate a mobile home or modular home in a
mobile home park or on a free-standing mobile home site, without first
obtaining a permit from the Town Board of Trustees for such purpose. All
applicants shall appear, either personally or by a duly authorized
representative, at a meeting of the Board of Trustees, at which time the
Trustees shall review the application.
      (2)   No permit shall be issued except after approval of the Board of
Trustees at such meeting.
   (C)   Application. All applications for permits to move or locate mobile
homes or modular homes in the town shall be made to the Town Clerk-Treasurer.
Such application shall be in writing and shall accurately state the route over
which the mobile home or modular home is proposed to be moved, and the proposed
new location thereof, giving the lot, block and addition, or legal description.
Such application shall further state the proposed date or dates for the moving
of such mobile home or modular home, and shall further state the height of the
home when loaded and whether it shall be necessary to raise, lower or cut any
wires or cable belonging to a public service corporation or the town, and make
any cuts or alterations in the paving or public streets in the town.
   (D)   Inspection. Prior to the issuance of a permit to locate a mobile home
within the corporate limits of the town, the Code Enforcement Official of the
town shall be afforded reasonable access to the mobile home to ascertain
whether unsafe conditions exist. Such official shall be afforded similar access
upon application by a person for renewal or extension of any permit provided by
this chapter. Such reasonable access to any mobile home shall not be denied to
the Code Enforcement Official.
   (E)   Fees. Fees for any license, permit or inspection herein provide shall
be set by the Town Board of Trustees, by resolution, and may be changes or
modified by resolution from time to time.
(Prior Code, § 12-314) Penalty, see §
151.99
§ 151.15 PERMITS NOT TRANSFERABLE.
   No permit granted pursuant to the provisions of this chapter shall be
transferable.
(Prior Code, § 12-315)
§ 151.16 VIOLATION AND APPEAL.
   Any violation of this chapter, state statutes or other applicable law shall
constitute cause for denial or revocation of any permit required herein;
provided, however, that upon denial or revocation of any permit, an appeal of
the Code Enforcement Official’s action may be taken to the Town Council by
filing a notice of appeal with the Code Enforcement Official and the Town
Clerk-Treasurer within ten days of the Code Enforcement Official’s action.
(Prior Code, § 12-316)
§ 151.17 RELIEF IN THE COURTS.
   No penalty imposed by and pursuant to this chapter shall interfere with the
right of the town also to apply to the proper courts of the state for a
mandamus, and injunction, or other appropriate action against such person, firm
or corporation.
(Prior Code, § 12-317)
§ 151.18 VIOLATION BY CORPORATE OFFICERS AND AGENTS.
   Violation of any of the terms or provision of this chapter by any
corporation or association shall subject the officers and agents actively in
charge of the business of such corporation or association, to the penalty
herein provided.
(Prior Code, § 12-318)
§ 151.99 PENALTY.
   Any person, firm or corporation found violating any provision of this
chapter shall, upon conviction, be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be
fined as provided in §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 12-319)
CHAPTER 152: STREETS AND SIDEWALKS
Section
   
152.01   Trees and obstruction of streets
   
152.02   Unlawful to injure trees and shrubbery
   
152.03   Unlawful obstructions
   
152.04   Unlawful to deposit trash upon the streets or sidewalks
   
152.05   Unlawful to play on streets
   
152.06   Vehicles not to be washed on street
   
152.07   Water, mud from vehicle not to drain into street
   
152.08   Water from filling stations and other businesses
   
152.09   Owner or occupant not to permit sidewalk or sidewalk area to become a
hazard
   
152.10   Street not to be obstructed so as to interfere with drainage
   
152.11   Pipeline construction under rights-of-way
   
152.12   Design criteria for streets
 
   
152.99   Penalty
§ 152.01 TREES AND OBSTRUCTION OF STREETS.
   (A)   The owner of any premises abutting on any street of this town shall
trim all trees and shrubbery growing in the parking, between the sidewalks and
the roadway, of any such street, and all trees and shrubbery growing on any
part of the premises adjacent to the sidewalks or any street or alley, in such
manner that the boughs or limbs thereof shall not obstruct free and convenient
passage and travel along the streets, sidewalks and alleys. When such premises
are occupied by some person other than the owner, such occupant shall trim the
trees and shrubbery in the same manner as hereinafter required of the owner.
Such trees and shrubbery shall be trimmed so that the lowest branches or
foliage shall not be lower than ten feet above the roadway of a street or
alley, nor lower than eight feet above the sidewalk.
   (B)   Any owner or occupant who shall fail, refuse or neglect to trim trees
and shrubbery as provided in division (A) above, after receiving five days’
notice from the head of the department in charge of streets to do so, shall be
guilty of an offense against the town. Every day that the owner or occupant
shall fail, refuse or neglect to trim the trees or shrubbery, after the
expiration of the five days’ notice, shall be a separate offense.
(Prior Code, § 14-101) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.02 UNLAWFUL TO INJURE TREES AND SHRUBBERY.
   It is unlawful for any person to injure any tree or shrubbery on a street or
alley in the town; provided, that this shall not prohibit the lawful and proper
care and removal of such trees and shrubbery.
(Prior Code, § 14-102) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.03 UNLAWFUL OBSTRUCTIONS.
   (A)   Merchandise. It is unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to
place upon or permit to be placed upon the sidewalks, parkways, streets and
alleys of the town any goods, wares, articles of merchandise or any other
obstruction, and leave same thereon; or to use the same as a place to carry on
a business or trade.
(Prior Code, § 14-103)
   (B)   Unlawful to obstruct unduly sidewalks and streets. It is unlawful for
any person, firm or corporation to use or obstruct the sidewalks of the town in
any manner so as to interfere unduly with pedestrian traffic thereon, or to use
or obstruct the streets and alleys of the town in any manner so as to interfere
unduly with lawful traffic and parking thereon.
(Prior Code, § 14-104)
Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.04 UNLAWFUL TO DEPOSIT TRASH UPON THE STREETS OR SIDEWALKS.
   It is unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to deposit, throw or
sweep into or upon the streets, alleys, parking or sidewalks of the town any
paper, rubbish, grass, weeds, tree trimmings, dirt, trash, crates, boxes or
other refuse of any kind.
(Prior Code, § 14-105) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.05 UNLAWFUL TO PLAY ON STREETS.
   It is unlawful for any person to play on the main-traveled portion of the
streets and alleys of the town, except as may be authorized by ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 14-106) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.06 VEHICLES NOT TO BE WASHED ON STREET.
   The washing of an automobile or other vehicle in any street of the town is
hereby prohibited.
(Prior Code, § 14-107) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.07 WATER, MUD FROM VEHICLE NOT TO DRAIN INTO STREET.
   No automobile or other vehicle shall be washed at any place within the town
where the water, dirt, mud or other substances removed therefrom by or during
the washing thereof, shall drain into or upon any street or sidewalk of the
town.
(Prior Code, § 14-108) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.08 WATER FROM FILLING STATIONS AND OTHER BUSINESSES.
   It is unlawful for any owner or operator of a filling station or other place
of business, or any agent or employee thereof, to cause or allow water, grease
or other fluid to flow or drain into, upon, over or across any sidewalk,
parking, street, alley or other public way.
(Prior Code, § 14-109) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.09 OWNER OR OCCUPANT NOT TO PERMIT SIDEWALK OR SIDEWALK AREA TO BECOME A
HAZARD.
   It is unlawful for the owner or occupant of property abutting upon a
sidewalk area to permit the sidewalk or sidewalk area adjacent to the property
to become a hazard to persons using the sidewalk, or sidewalk area.
(Prior Code, § 14-110) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.10 STREET NOT TO BE OBSTRUCTED SO AS TO INTERFERE WITH DRAINAGE.
   It is unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to obstruct any street,
sidewalk or alley, by placing any approach driveway or other obstruction or
substance whatever that will obstruct or prevent the natural flow of water,
into the storm sewers or drains, or dam the same so as to back any water upon
the streets, alleys, sidewalks or gutter.
(Prior Code, § 14-111) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.11 PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION UNDER RIGHTS-OF-WAY.
   (A)   A permit must be obtained from the Board of Trustees subsequent to the
construction of any petroleum product pipeline under the surface of streets,
alleys and other public ways within the town.
   (B)   (1)   Construction drawings must be submitted as a part of any
application for such permit. The pipeline shall be laid to a minimum depth of
three feet from the top of the pipeline or land surfaces, and all pavements
shall be restored to their original condition according to all specifications
after the work is completed on any segment of the pipeline.
      (2)   “As built” drawings shall be furnished to the town by the pipeline
company to show the precise locations, depths and the nature of all materials
installed in accordance with the permit.
   (C)   The pipeline company shall indemnify the town and hold the town
harmless from any loss or costs due to any claim or liability resulting from
construction or maintenance of the system or from operation of the pipeline in
any way. The pipeline company will hold the town harmless from any litigation
costs and attorneys’ fees incurred as a result of any construction, maintenance
or operation of the system.
   (D)   Wherever the line is to be put under any pavement without opening the
pavement, the line shall be run through a tunnel cased in accordance with
specifications to be approved by the town, adequate to support the pavement and
to support the traffic on the pavement.
   (E)   At least 45 days’ notice shall be given to the town before any new
construction work is scheduled on any street, alley or other public way on the
pipeline covered by this permit. The pipeline company will coordinate with the
town to assure that its construction work will not conflict with work scheduled
by the town.
   (F)   (1)   All work to be done under the provisions of this chapter shall
be performed in a good and workmanlike manner with materials suited for the
purpose, and full compliance with the provisions of all federal laws, state
laws and town ordinances relating construction.
      (2)   No sewer main or other town property shall be damaged in any way by
the pipeline company, and if any such town factory is damaged in violation of
this section, the repair of the damage; provided, that at the option of the
town it may notify the pipeline company to make the repairs promptly at the
pipeline company’s expense and the pipeline company shall thereupon perform all
the required repairs to the town’s specifications at the pipeline company’s
expense.
   (G)   Repairs or replacement of the pipeline by or in behalf of the pipeline
company may be initiated only after contact and or consultation with town
officials. All land surfaces and all pavements shall be restored to their
original condition according to specifications furnished by the town.
   (H)   (1)   The pipeline company shall maintain and operate the pipeline in
a safe manner at all times. The pipeline company shall, periodically, visually
inspect the pipeline for leaks using the most reliable equipment available for
that purpose. These inspections shall be made by the company not less often
than once every week.
      (2)   The written results of such inspections shall be forwarded to the
Board of Trustees on a quarterly basis.
   (I)   In consideration of the rights granted by a new construction/repair or
replacement permit, the pipeline company shall pay the town the sum of a
minimum of $100 at the time of accepting such permit.
(Prior Code, § 14-201)
§ 152.12 DESIGN CRITERIA FOR STREETS.
   (A)   Generally. Streets shall include earthwork, proper subgrade, base
course(s), wearing surface, concrete curb and gutters, proper backfill and
proper drainage structures, including storm sewers and inlets. A maintenance
bond or irrevocable letter of credit shall be posted in an amount equal to 100%
of the determined amount of construction costs for a two-year period.
   (B)   Plan sheets and profiles.
      (1)   All intersections, culs-de-sac and other critical locations shall
be shown in plan detail at a minimum scale of one inch equals 20 feet,
including direction of drainage, top of curb elevation at PCs, PTs and high or
low points. All curve information and drainage structures shall be shown in
detail.
      (2)   All drainage areas shall be clearly marked on the drainage area
plan sheet; showing acreage, runoff and off-site pickup points.
      (3)   A site plan showing proposed locations and elevations of all
utilities shall accompany the street and storm sewer plans.
      (4)   The profile may be either three separate profiles or one single
profile.
         (a)   Three separate profiles. When using three separate profiles, the
top and bottom shall show existing property line and proposed top of curb. The
middle profile shall show only existing centerline profile. Stationing shall be
along the centerline.
         (b)   One single profile. When using one single profile, both property
lines shall be shown along with the proposed top of curb. The centerline
profile shall not be shown. Stationing shall be along the centerline.
      (5)   All fill areas within the street right-of-way shall be cross-
hatched on the profile, and notation shall be made that the fill area shall be
compacted to a minimum of 95% standard proctor density. When storm sewer pipes
are located in fill area, the fill shall be made and compacted to finish grade,
then trenched for storm drain excavation.
      (6)   Curb returns with elevations shall be clearly labeled on profile.
      (7)   Vertical curves in profile shall give the top of curb elevation at
the PC, PI, PT and high or low point, at a minimum of 50 feet intervals.
      (8)   Storm sewers shall be located along centerline of streets unless
otherwise approved by the Town Engineer.
   (C)   Streets.
      (1)   Width of streets shall be according to the classifications as
follows. Width shall be measured from curb face to curb face or from edge of
design strength pavement.
 
  Commercial and industrial40 feet
Residential collector       36 feet
Residential (local)         26 feet
 
      (2)   All streets shall be constructed with concrete curbs.
      (3)   The centerline of paving shall be the centerline of right-of-way
where dedication has been made according to the major street plan.
      (4)   The minimum grade set along the curb shall be 0.5%. The maximum
desirable grade for non-arterial streets shall be limited to 8%. For situations
where the topography is unusually hilly, grades will be permitted up to a
maximum of 12% providing they do not exceed 500 feet in length from PT to PC.
      (5)   The grade of the curb returns will continue for the full arc on all
intersections where a midway opposing break is not provided.
      (6)   Design speed shall be 25 mph on all residential streets and 30 mph
on all collector streets.
       (7)   For horizontal curves, the minimum centerline radius on street
alignment shall be 125 feet.
      (8)   The minimum radius on returns at residential intersections shall be
25 feet. At intersections of a residential and arterial street, the minimum
radius on returns shall be 30 feet. At intersections of arterial streets, the
minimum radius on returns shall be 40 feet. The minimum radius on the returns
for industrial districts shall be 40 feet.
      (9)   The maximum grade of a residential street when intersecting an
arterial shall be 2% for a minimum of 100 feet from the curb line of the
arterial. No vertical curve shall begin any closer than 50 feet from the curb
line of the arterial. The maximum grade of residential streets at intersections
shall be 4%.
      (10)   A proposed and existing profile shall be shown beyond the end of
all dead-end streets for a minimum of 200 feet to determine a satisfactory
grade for future development.
      (11)   Cross slope may be one-fourth inch or three-eighths inch per foot;
however, crown will be flattened off so that crown never exceeds curb height.
      (12)   Proposed streets shall intersect one another as nearly at right
angles as topography and other limiting design factors permit.
      (13)   Proposed developments of residential areas shall keep to a minimum
the use of four-way intersections.
   (D)   Typical sections.
      (1)   Typical sections shall be drawn at the same horizontal and vertical
scale.
      (2)   Typical sections shall show dimensions, type of materials, layer
details, reserve topsoil, temporary and permanent erosion control, compacted
thickness and the like.
      (3)   All typical sections or notes that are necessary to clearly reflect
the design shall be included.
      (4)   The developer shall provide soil tests for all areas to be paved.
Soil tests will be submitted to the Town Engineer for approval. If soil tests
indicate that the soil has a plasticity index of ten or greater, a minimum of
six inches of subgrade shall be modified with a minimum of 5% hydrated lime by
weight or Class III fly ash. If the soil tests indicate that the soil is
granular and unstable, the method of stabilization shall be approved by the
Town Engineer. If desired, subgrade may be built of an approved borrow
material.
      (5)   Industrial and commercial pavement sections shall be a minimum of
ten-inch asphaltic concrete or eight-inch Portland cement concrete. Residential
pavement sections shall be a minimum of six and one-half inch asphaltic
concrete or six-inch Portland cement concrete.
      (6)   Pavement sections for secondary and primary arterial streets shall
be furnished by the Town Engineer’s office.
      (7)   Portland cement concrete streets shall have an integrally placed
curb of the same mix design as for street paving. The curb shall be a minimum
of six inches wide at the top and curb face shall be a minimum of six inches in
height exclusive of bottom fillet.
      (8)   Joints in Portland cement concrete paving, curbs and gutters shall
be placed in accordance with the Town Engineer’s recommendation.
      (9)   Asphaltic concrete streets shall have a Portland cement concrete
curb and gutter. The curb shall not be less than six inches wide at the top
with a six-inch face in height exclusive of bottom fillet and the gutter shall
be a minimum of 18 inches in width.
      (10)   Asphaltic concrete shall be Types A, B and C per the State
Department of Transportation Standard Specifications for Highway Construction.
      (11)   Where Residential Estate (RE) zoning has been allowed, the typical
roadway section may be a minimum of six inches of stabilized aggregate base on
compacted subgrade with three inches of asphaltic concrete surface.
   (E)   Sidewalks.
      (1)   Sidewalks shall be required on both sides of local and collector
streets.
      (2)   All sidewalks shall be of Portland cement concrete. Sidewalks shall
include pedestrian bridges across creeks and streams where applicable.
      (3)   The finished thickness of Portland cement concrete sidewalks shall
not be less than four inches, and the width shall be not less than four feet.
      (4)   In general, sidewalks shall be constructed within the dedicated
right-of-way at a distance not less than one foot from the abutting property
lines, and except at intersections or as approved by the town, shall be no less
than three feet from the outside curb line of the street pavements.
      (5)   Sidewalks must provide personable access for the safe and
convenient movement across curbs of physically handicapped persons, including
those persons in wheelchairs. Wheelchair ramps shall be constructed in
accordance with standard details provided by the Town Engineer’s office.
   (F)   Stormwater drainage criteria. All stormwater runoff shall be subject
to review and approval by the Town Engineer with regard to analysis, design and
construction of drainage facilities. The appropriate public authority shall
have the right to maintain or to cause to be maintained the drainage system for
its intended purposes.
   (G)   Adoption of state standards. The latest edition of the state Standard
Specifications for Highway Construction, as published by the State Department
of Transportation, are hereby adopted as the standard specifications for
grading, street, road and drainage construction for the town, except as amended
herein. In the event of any conflict between any of the provisions of the State
Standard Specifications for Highway Construction and the specific provisions
set forth herein, then in such event the specific provisions set forth herein
shall control.
(Prior Code, § 14-301)
§ 152.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person, firm or corporation who violates any provision of this
chapter for which no specific penalty is prescribed shall be guilty of an
offense and, upon conviction thereof, shall be fined as provided in §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 14-112)
   (B)   Any person who violates any provision of §
152.11 shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be
fined as provided in §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 14-202)
