GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 153.01 OIL AND GAS DRILLING UNLAWFUL.
   It is hereby declared unlawful for any person or other entity to engage in
the drilling of oil and gas wells within the corporate limits of the town.
(Prior Code, § 12-501) Penalty, see §
153.99
§ 153.02 SPECIAL EXCEPTIONS.
   The Town Board of Trustees may grant special exceptions to the prohibition
contained in §
153.01 and may authorize the issuance of a permit to allow the drilling of oil
and gas wells within the corporate limits of the town according to the terms
and conditions of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 12-502)
§ 153.03 OIL AND GAS INSPECTOR.
   The town shall retain an oil and gas inspector who is knowledgeable in the
field to perform all inspections required and to review all information
submitted with any application and to enforce the provisions of this chapter.
The inspector is hereby empowered to revoke any such permit and thereby to
cause all operations to cease as he or she deems necessary in the process of
enforcing this chapter. In addition to the oil and gas inspector, the Board of
Trustees may engage the services of other professionals, including, but not
limited to, petroleum engineers, hydrologists and geologists, whose advice
shall be sought as needed during the application process.
(Prior Code, § 12-503)
§ 153.04 FEES.
   The town shall assess fees as set by motion or resolution in order to offset
the cost of performing the duties and responsibilities created hereby.
(Prior Code, § 12-504)
REGULATIONS
§ 153.15 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning. All
technical or oil and gas words or phrases used herein and not specifically
defined herein shall have that meaning customarily attributable thereto by
prudent operators in the oil and gas industry.
   LEASE. Any tract of land subject to an oil, gas and mineral lease or other
oil and gas development contract, or any unit composed of several tracts and
leased but operated as one lease, and any tract of land in which the minerals
are owned by an operator but which, due to the fee royalty ownership is
developed and operated as a separate tract.
   PERMITTEE. The person to whom is issued a permit for the drilling and
operation of a well, and his, her or its administrators, executors, heirs,
successors and assigns.
   PERSON. Includes both the singular and the plural; and means any person,
individual, firm, partnership, association, corporation, club, society,
cooperative, trust, municipal corporation or political subdivision whatsoever.
   RIG-UP. The process of setting up equipment and machinery for drilling
operations.
   WELL. Any hole or holes, bore or bores, to any sand, formation, strata or
depth for the purpose of producing and recovering any oil, gas, liquid
hydrocarbon or any of them.
(Prior Code, § 12-511)
§ 153.16 PERMIT.
   (A)   No permit shall be granted by the oil and gas inspector until the
Board of Trustees shall have granted a special exception as set forth in this
chapter.
   (B)   The permit shall:
      (1)   Embody all standard conditions specified herein and any special
conditions required by the Board of Trustees;
      (2)   Contain the total depth to which the well may be drilled; and
      (3)   Contain and specify that no operations shall be commenced until
permittee shall file and have approved an indemnity bond in the designated
principal amount as so determined by the Board of Trustees and conditioned a
specified in §
153.17.
(Prior Code, § 12-512)
§ 153.17 PERMITTEES INSURANCE AND BOND.
   (A)   In the event a special exception is granted by the Board of Trustees
for the drilling and operation of a well, no permit shall be issued until the
permittee shall file with the Town Clerk-Treasurer a bond and a certificate of
insurance as follows.
      (1)   (a)   A bond in the principal sum as has been so determined by the
Town Board of Trustees, but not to be less than $50,000 per well nor more than
$100,000 per operator, the bond to be executed by a reliable insurance company
authorized to do business in the state as surety, and with applicant as
principal, returning to the town for the benefit of the town and all persons
concerned. The bond shall become effective on or before the date the same is
filed with the Town Clerk-Treasurer and shall remain in force and effect for at
least a period of six months subsequent to the receipt of certified plugging
records.
         (b)   It shall be the duty of the applicant to maintain the bond in
full force and effect for such period of time and in the event of cancellation
at any time the special exception permit or permits granted to applicant based
upon such bond shall be automatically revoked. The cancellation of the bond
will be conditioned on the permittee promptly paying all fines, penalties and
other assessments imposed upon permittee by reason of his or her breach of any
of the terms, provisions and conditions of the permit, and that the permittee
will promptly restore the streets and sidewalks and other public property of
the town, which may be disturbed or damaged in the operations, to their former
condition; and that the permittee will promptly clear all premises of all
litter, trash, waste and other substances used, allowed or occurring in the
drilling or producing operations, and will, after abandonment, grade, level and
restore the property to the same surface condition, as nearly as possible, as
existed when operations for the drilling of the well or wells first commenced;
and that the permittee will indemnify and hold the town harmless from any and
all liability growing out of or attributable to the granting of such permit.
         (c)   If at any time the Town Board of Trustees shall deem any
permittee’s bond to be insufficient for any reason, it may require the
permittee to file a new bond.
      (2)   (a)   In addition to the bond required in division (A)(1) above,
the permittee shall carry a policy or policies of standard comprehensive public
liability insurance, including contractual liability covering bodily injuries
and property damage, naming the permittee and the town as insureds with an
insurance company authorized to do business within the state. The policy or
policies in the aggregate shall provide for the following minimum coverage.
 
Bodily injuries per person $250,000
Per accident               $500,000
Property damage            $200,000
 
         (b)   Permittee shall file with the Town Clerk-Treasurer certificates
of the insurance as above stated, and shall obtain the written approval thereof
by the Town Clerk-Treasurer, who shall act thereon within ten days from the
date of such filing. The insurance policy or policies shall not be cancelled
without written notice to the Town Clerk-Treasurer at least 30 days prior to
the effective date of such cancellation. In the event the policy or policies
are cancelled, the permit granted shall terminate, and the permittee’s rights
to operate under the permit shall cease until permittee files additional
insurance as provided herein.
   (B)   If, after completion of a well, the permittee has complied with all of
the provisions of this chapter, such as to removing derrick, clearing premises
and the like, he or she may apply to the Town Board of Trustees to have the
insurance policies reduced as follows for the remainder of the time the well
produces without reworking. During any reworking operations, the amount of the
insurance policy or policies shall be increased back to the original amounts.
 
Bodily injuries per person $50,000
Per accident               $100,000
Property damage            $50,000
 
(Prior Code, § 12-513)
§ 153.18 DEEPER DRILLING.
   Once any well has either been completed as a producer or abandoned as a dry
hole, it shall be a violation of this chapter for any person to drill such well
a deeper depth than that reached in the prior drilling operations without the
permittee as to such well obtaining a new permit after filing an application.
(Prior Code, § 12-514) Penalty, see §
153.99
§ 153.19 DERRICK AND RIG.
   It shall be a violation of this chapter for any person to use or operate in
connection with the drilling or reworking of any well within the corporate
limits of the town any wooden derrick or any steam-powered rig, and all engines
shall be equipped with adequate mufflers approved by the oil and gas inspector.
It shall further be a violation of this chapter to permit any drilling rig or
derrick to remain on the premises or drilling site for a period longer than 60
days after completion or abandonment of any well. At all times from the start
of erection of a derrick, or a mast, or a gin-pole, until the well is abandoned
and plugged or cased as a producer and enclosed with a fence as herein
provided, the permittee shall keep a watch person on duty on the premises at
all times; provided, however, that it shall not be necessary to keep an extra
watchperson on duty on the premises when other workers or permittee are on the
premises. The location of such hole to be a minimum distance of 25 feet from
any existing sewer main.
(Prior Code, § 12-515) Penalty, see §
153.99
§ 153.20 PITS.
   Either earthen or steel slush pits shall be permitted in connection with the
drilling operation, and pits are to be made impermeable if, in the opinion of
the oil and gas inspector, the drilling fluid requires it. In the event a steel
pit is used, the pit and its contents shall be removed from the premises and
the drilling site within 30 days after completion of the well. In the event an
earthen slush pit is used, same shall be filled and leveled within 180 days
after completion of the well. Such pits shall not be located within 20 feet of
an existing sanitary sewer, or 25 feet from the street right-of-way line.
(Prior Code, § 12-516)
§ 153.21 CASING.
   All casing must be of a grade quality commonly used by the industry in
similar conditions.
(Prior Code, § 12-517)
§ 153.22 SETTING AND CEMENTING CASING.
   No well shall be drilled within the town without properly setting surface
casing to a minimum depth of 400 feet, subject to control of the State
Corporation Commission. No well shall be drilled within the corporate limits of
the town without cementing the surface casing by the pump and plug method with
sufficient cement to completely fill all the annular space behind such casing
to surface ground; and without cementing the production string by the pump and
plug method with sufficient cement to completely fill all the annular space
behind the production string to at least 400 feet above the highest oil or gas
bearing horizon, subject to control of the State Corporation Commission.
(Prior Code, § 12-518)
§ 153.23 BLOW-OUT PREVENTERS.
   No well shall be drilled within the corporate limits of the town without
being; properly equipped without blow-out preventers. Nor will drilling fluid
other than drilling “mud” of sufficiently high density to control natural gas
flows be used without first demonstrating either that such “blow-out”
conditions are unlikely or that suitable safeguards have been provided to
ensure safe drilling conditions at all times.
(Prior Code, § 12-519)
§ 153.24 DRILL STEM TESTS.
   It shall be unlawful and an offense for any person in connection with the
drilling or reworking operation of any well within the corporate limits of the
town to take and to complete any drill stem test or tests except during
daylight hours, and then only if the well effluent during the test is produced
through an adequate oil and gas separator to storage tanks, and the effluent
remaining in the drill pipe at the time the tool is closed is flushed to the
surface by circulating drilling fluid down the annuals and up the drill pipe.
(Prior Code, § 12-520) Penalty, see §
153.99
§ 153.25 PREMISES TO BE KEPT CLEAN AND SANITARY.
   The premises shall be kept in a clean and sanitary condition, free from
rubbish of every character, to the satisfaction of the town staff, at all times
during drilling operations or reworking operations are being conducted and as
long thereafter as oil or gas is being produced therefrom.
(Prior Code, § 12-521)
§ 153.26 POWER.
   After completion of drilling operations, motive power for all operations
shall be electric only.
(Prior Code, § 12-522)
§ 153.27 STORAGE TANKS AND SEPARATORS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful and an offense for any person to use, construct
or operate in connection with any producing well within the corporate limits of
the town, any crude oil storage tanks except to the extent of two low-type
steel tanks for all storage, not exceeding 500 barrels capacity for each well
connected thereto, and so constructed and maintained as to be vapor-tight and
properly vented. A permittee may use, construct and operate a conventional
steel separator, vapor recovery unit and such other approved tanks and
appurtenances as are necessary for treating oil with each of the facilities to
be so constructed and maintained as to be vapor-tight. Each oil/gas separator
shall be equipped with both a regulation pressure relief safety valve and
bursting head. All such tanks shall be placed above ground, and the tanks shall
be placed upon a suitable earth or concrete pad. All tubing for the tanks and
separators shall be made of internally plastic-coated steel.
   (B)   The use of a central tank battery is permitted so long as not more
than two tanks as specified in division (A) above are used for each well
connected to the battery.
   (C)   The tank or tanks shall be enclosed within a conventional type
firewall constructed of compacted earth and sufficient water shall be used
during the firewall construction to assure adequate compaction.
subject to control of the State Corporation Commission.
   (D)   An oil/gas separator shall be equipped with both a regulation pressure
relief safety valve and bursting head. All such tanks shall be placed above
ground, and the tanks shall be placed upon a suitable earth or concrete pad.
All tubing for the tanks and separators shall be made of internally plastic-
coated steel.
   (E)   The use of a central tank battery is permitted so long as not more
than two tanks as specified in division (D) above are used for each well
connected to the battery.
   (F)   The tank or tanks shall be enclosed within a conventional type
firewall constructed of compacted earth and sufficient water shall be used
during the firewall construction to assure adequate compaction.
   (G)   The firewall enclosing the tank shall have a minimum capacity equal to
two times the volume of the tanks enclosed.
   (H)   The tanks shall be within the firewall and shall be fenced and
landscaped to assure them of being practically unseen when viewed from outside
the fenced or landscaped enclosure.
   (I)   The separators shall be installed in a manner that will assure them of
being practically unseen when viewed from outside the fenced or landscaped
enclosure.
   (J)   No tanks or separators shall be located closer than 300 feet to a
dwelling, business structure, school or street without the permittee having
first secured the written permission of the owner or owners thereof; except
that no storage tank or separator shall be located nearer than 400 feet from a
property line of a residential subdivision.
   (K)   All petroleum flow lines shall be either steel pipe or thread
connected fiber glass pipe certified 1,000 psi test according to A.P.I.
(American Petroleum Institute).
(Prior Code, § 12-523) Penalty, see §
153.99
§ 153.28 FENCING.
   Any person who completes any well as a producer shall have the obligation to
enclose the well, together with its surface facilities and storage tanks, by a
substantial, smooth new wire fence sufficiently high and properly built so as
to ordinarily keep persons and animals out of the enclosure with all gates
thereon to be kept locked when permittee or his or her employees are not within
the enclosure.
(Prior Code, § 12-524)
§ 153.29 VENTING AND FLARING OF GAS.
   No person engaged in drilling or operating any well shall permit gas to
escape or be vented into the air unless the gas be flared and burned. All gas
flared or burned from a torch, pipe or any other burning device, within the
corporate limits of the town must be done in such a manner so as not to
constitute a fire hazard to any property and the location of the torch, pipe or
other burning device, the construction thereof, the maintenance thereof and the
operation thereof, shall at all times be in full compliance with such
regulations as may from time to time be issued by the oil and gas inspector of
the town.
(Prior Code, § 12-525) Penalty, see §
153.99
§ 153.30 DISPOSAL OF SALTWATER.
   Permittee shall make adequate provisions for the disposal of all saltwater
or other impurities which may be brought to the surface, such disposal to be
made in such manner as to not contaminate the water supply, present or
prospective, or to injure surface vegetation. Such saltwater disposal shall be
accomplished with the use of fiberglass pipe or plastic pipe (SDR-7 or equal)
with tracer wire installed in the ditch at the time of construction. The depth
of such saltwater disposal line to be a minimum of 36 inches.
(Prior Code, § 12-526)
§ 153.31 PROHIBITION AGAINST USE OF SEWER SYSTEM.
   No person engaged in drilling or operating any well shall permit the use of
the sewer system of the town for the purpose of discharging any deleterious
substance resulting from any such oil or gas activities into the sewer system,
No drill site shall be located within 25 feet of any existing sanitary sewer
main or 25 feet from the street right-of-way line.
(Prior Code, § 12-527) Penalty, see §
153.99
§ 153.32 VIOLATION OF STATE OF FEDERAL LAWS OR REGULATIONS.
   Any laws of the state or any rules, regulations or requirements of any state
or federal regulatory body having jurisdiction. In reference to drilling,
completing, equipping, operating, producing, maintaining or abandoning an oil
or gas well or related appurtenances, equipment or facilities, or in reference
to firewalls, fire protection, blowout protection or convenience of persons or
property, shall also be a part of this chapter and shall be enforced with like
effect with the other provisions hereof.
(Prior Code, § 12-528) Penalty, see §
153.99
PROCEDURES
§ 153.45 SPECIAL EXCEPTION PROCEDURES FOR OIL AND GAS PERMITS.
   (A)   These procedures are designed to provide a quick but thorough method
by which the town can make an informed decision. In each case, the issue before
the Board of Trustees is whether a specific drilling proposal by reason of its
proximity to urban settings and of its physical character, represents a
detriment to the public health, safety and welfare. If the proposal does not
represent a detriment, the Board of Trustees will grant a special exception
authorizing the issuance of a permit to engage in whatever phase of activity
has been requested. The permit will embody all standard conditions set forth in
§§
153.15 through
153.32 and any additional conditions which are deemed necessary by the Board of
Trustees relating to a particular permit.
   (B)   If the proposal does represent a detriment, and conditions of
operation cannot sufficiently mitigate the detriment, the request for a special
exception will be denied. In any event, the permit process shall proceed as set
forth in this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 12-531)
§ 153.46 DRILLING PHASE.
   (A)   The applicant shall contact the Town Clerk-Treasurer or oil and gas
inspector for a pre-application conference in order to become familiar with the
process.
   (B)   The applicant shall complete the application for oil and gas drilling
and operations. This application must be accompanied by a site plan with
information as required in §§
153.15 through
153.32 and a route map which will be supplied by the town. The application will
also be accompanied by a list of the names and mailing addresses of all of the
property owners within a 600-foot radius of the proposed well. The list shall
show the names and the last known addresses of all such property owners as
shown by the current year’s tax rolls in the office of the County Treasurer.
The application fee is required to be submitted at this time.
   (C)   The town staff will advise the applicant of the date of the hearing
before the Board of Trustees and of the standard conditions which are
automatically imposed, should the exception be granted. The staff shall set the
application for a hearing before the Board of Trustees which shall be within 30
days of receipt of completed forms. The staff shall mail a public notice of
hearing to property owners as provided by the applicant and shall cause the
notice to be published in a legal newspaper located in the county, all at least
ten days in advance of the meeting. A sign shall be posted at the closest
public location near the subject parcel. The notice shall indicate the nature
of the request, the name of the applicant, a general location of the proposed
well and the specific legal description. It will also contain information
regarding the date, time and location of the hearing as well as the phone
number for the town representative from which access to additional information
may be obtained. The staff shall prepare recommendations regarding the
application as requested by the Board of Trustees.
   (D)   The Board of Trustees will hear the application and approve the
request with standard conditions or special conditions as may be appropriate or
deny the application. In no case will the Board of Trustees table or continue
action upon the request for a period in excess of 40 days from the date of the
first hearing. At this time, the applicant will post bond and supply insurance
binders in accordance with the terms of §§
153.15 through
153.32. After approval of the exception by the Board of Trustees, and upon
receipt of the bonds and insurance binders, the oil and gas inspector will
issue a permit to drill, deepen or plug back which permit will specify the
standard conditions and any special conditions. Such permit shall be issued
within two working days of the granting of special exception. The operator
shall notify the town staff of his or her intention to “rig-up” within 24 hours
of commencement.
   (E)   If the applicant should fail to begin operations within 90 days from
the date of approval, or if the applicant ceases to operate for a period of 90
consecutive days, the well shall enter dormant well status. Dormant well status
will continue until the operator receives permission to recommence operations,
until the permit is revoked or until the well is properly abandoned. In no case
may operations on a dormant well recommence until the oil and gas inspector
officially removes a permit from dormant status. The oil and gas inspector
shall make an administrative determination as to whether conditions have
changed sufficiently to warrant reconsideration of the permit. If conditions
have changed sufficiently, the permit shall be placed upon the agenda for the
next regular meeting of the Board of Trustees for reconsideration. If
conditions have not changed sufficiently from the time of the granting of the
permit to warrant its reconsideration, the oil and gas inspector may remove the
permit from dormant well status and allow operations to recommence.
   (F)   Comprehensive programs which involve the drilling of several wells may
be entertained at one time by the Board of Trustees and separate permits may be
issued for each well in the program at one time. Wells within a recognized and
approved comprehensive drilling program which are directly dependent upon the
function of other wells within the comprehensive program, shall enjoy an
indefinite period from the time of the granting of the permit until
commencement of the well drilling and operations. During such period, such well
shall not be given dormant status so long as the comprehensive drilling and
production program is diligently pursued to completion. The applicant in such
cases must demonstrate to the oil and gas inspector that they are pursuing a
timely schedule for the completion of the program. If the town staff or any
member of the Board of Trustees observes little or no effort being made to
complete a comprehensive drilling program for any extended period of time, they
may recommend to the Board of Trustees that the balance of the permits yet to
be commenced be reconsidered for dormant status or revocation.
   (G)   The permit shall be posted in a clearly visible location at the well
site and the oil and gas inspector will make inspections as necessary during
the drilling phase.
   (H)   When the applicant nears the point of setting surface casing, he or
she shall notify the town staff of his or her intent to set surface casing in
order to allow the oil and gas inspector the opportunity to observe the
cementing of the casing.
   (I)   Upon termination of the drilling phase, the applicant will notify the
town staff of termination of the drilling phase.
(Prior Code, § 12-532)
§ 153.47 COMPLETION PHASE.
   (A)   The applicant shall complete the well as necessary in accordance with
all required conditions. The completion phase occurs after drilling equipment
has been moved off site and the well is being prepared for production or
injection.
   (B)   The oil and gas inspector shall inspect during the completion phase as
necessary to ensure compliance with the permit.
   (C)   Upon the termination of the completion phase, the applicant shall
notify the town staff of termination of the completion phase. This will serve
as notice to the oil and gas inspector that he or she will need to inspect a
completed producing or injecting well site or, in the event the well is not
completed to the satisfaction of the applicant, that the abandonment phase will
soon initiate. A copy of State Corporation Commission Form 1002-A shall also be
submitted at this time and the oil and gas inspector shall complete an
inspection report, drilling and completion.
(Prior Code, § 12-533)
§ 153.48 OPERATIONAL PHASE.
   The applicant shall operate within the confines of the permit. The oil and
gas inspector performs annual inspections near the anniversary date of the
termination of the completion phase and other inspections as necessary and
notes them on an inspection report, operation phase.
(Prior Code, § 12-534)
§ 153.49 ABANDONMENT.
   The applicant shall submit a copy of State Corporation Commission Form No.
1003 to the office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer which will serve as notice of
the abandonment of the well site. The oil and gas inspector shall perform a
final inspection to determine whether the site has been reclaimed as required
by the permit. If he or she is satisfied of compliance, he or she will so note
on an inspection permit abandonment, a copy of which will be made available to
the applicant. If the oil and gas inspector is not satisfied of compliance, he
or she will so note on the inspection report along with the reasons therefor.
Within six months after approval of abandonment on the final inspection, the
inspector will notify the applicant that the well site has been reclaimed
sufficiently and that surety and insurance will no longer be required.
(Prior Code, § 12-535)
§ 153.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any violation of this chapter shall constitute an offense against the
town and any person, firm or corporation violating any of the terms or
provisions hereof shall, upon conviction thereof, be punished as provided in §
10.99. Failure to comply with the provisions hereof shall be deemed a
continuing offense, and each day’s continuance of failure to comply herewith
shall constitute a separate and distinct offense.
(Prior Code, § 12-505)
   (B)   Nothing contained herein shall be construed so as to preclude the town
from seeking injunctive relief, damages or any other remedies to enforce the
terms and conditions of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 12-506)
CHAPTER 154: FLOOD HAZARD PREVENTION
Section
   
154.01   Statement of purpose
   
154.02   Finding of facts
   
154.03   Methods of reducing flood losses
   
154.04   Definitions
   
154.05   Application; compliance; interpretation
   
154.06   Basis for establishing the areas of special flood hazard
   
154.07   Development permit required
   
154.08   Warning and disclaimer of liability
   
154.09   Designation of Building Inspector; duties
   
154.10   Permit procedures; approval or denial
   
154.11   Variance procedures
   
154.12   General standards; flood hazard areas
   
154.13   Specific standards; flood hazard areas
   
154.14   Standards for subdivision proposals; flood hazard areas
§ 154.01 STATEMENT OF PURPOSE.
   It is the purpose of this chapter to promote the public health, safety and
general welfare and to minimize public and private losses due to flood
conditions in specific areas by provisions designed to:
   (A)   Protect human life and health;
   (B)   Minimize expenditure of public money for costly flood control
projects;
   (C)   Minimize the need for rescue and relief efforts associated with
flooding and generally undertaken at the expense of the general public;
   (D)   Minimize prolonged business interruptions;
   (E)   Minimize damage to public facilities and utilities such as water and
gas mains, electric, telephone and sewer lines, streets and bridges located in
floodplains;
   (F)   Help maintain a stable tax base by providing for the sound use and
development of flood-prone areas in such a manner as to minimize future flood
blight areas; and
   (G)   Ensure potential buyers are notified that property is in a flood area.
(Prior Code, § 12-201)
§ 154.02 FINDING OF FACTS.
   The flood hazard areas of the town are subject to periodic inundation which
results in loss of life and property, health and safety hazards, disruption of
commerce and governmental services and extraordinary public expenditures for
flood protection and relief, all of which adversely affect the public health,
safety and general welfare. These flood losses are created by the cumulative
effect of obstructions in floodplains which cause an increase in flood heights
and velocities, and by the occupancy of flood hazard areas by uses vulnerable
to floods and hazardous to other lands because they are inadequately elevated,
floodproofed or otherwise protected from flood damage.
(Prior Code, § 12-202)
§ 154.03 METHODS OF REDUCING FLOOD LOSSES.
   In order to accomplish its purposes, these regulations are established to:
   (A)   Restrict or prohibit uses that are dangerous to health, safety or
property in times of flood or cause excessive increases in flood heights or
velocities;
   (B)   Require that uses vulnerable to floods, including facilities which
serve such uses, be protected against flood damage at the time of initial
construction;
   (C)   Control the alteration of natural floodplains, stream channels and
natural protective barriers, which are involved in the accommodation of
floodwaters;
   (D)   Control filling, grading, dredging and other development which may
increase flood damage; and
   (E)   Prevent or regulate the construction of flood barriers which will
increase flood hazards to other lands.
(Prior Code, § 12-203)
§ 154.04 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   APPEAL. A request for a review of an interpretation by the Town Board of
Trustees or its designated agency of any provision of this chapter or a request
for a variance.
   AREA OF SHALLOW FLOODING. A designated AO Zone on a community’s flood
insurance rate map (FIRM) with base flood depths from one to three feet. This
condition occurs where a clearly defined channel does not exist, where the path
of flooding is unpredictable and indeterminate, and where velocity flow may be
evident.
   AREA OF SPECIAL FLOOD HAZARD. The land in the floodplain within a community
subject to a 1% or greater chance of flooding in any given year.
   BASE FLOOD. The flood having a 1% chance of being equaled or exceeded in any
given year.
   DEVELOPMENT. Any human-made change to improved or unimproved real estate,
including, but not limited to, buildings or other structures, mining, dredging,
filling, grading, paving, excavation or drilling operations.
   EXISTING MOBILE HOME PARK OR MOBILE HOME SUBDIVISION. A parcel (or
contiguous parcels) of land divided into two or more mobile home lots for rent
or sale for which the construction of facilities for servicing the lot on which
the mobile home is to be affixed (including, at a minimum, the installation of
utilities, either final site grading or the pouring of concrete pads, and the
construction of streets) is completed before the original effective date of
this chapter.
   EXPANSION TO AN EXISTING MOBILE HOME PARK OR MOBILE HOME SUBDIVISION. The
preparation of additional sites by the construction of facilities for servicing
the lots on which the mobile homes are to be affixed (including the
installation of utilities, either final site grading or pouring of concrete
pads, or the construction of streets).
   FLOOD OR FLOODING. A general and temporary condition of partial or complete
inundation of normally dry land areas from:
      (1)   The overflow of inland or tidal waters; or
      (2)   The unusual and rapid accumulation of runoff of surface waters from
any source.
 
   FLOOD HAZARD BOUNDARY MAP (FHBM). An official map of a community, issued by
the Federal Insurance Administration, where the areas within the boundaries of
special flood hazards have been designated as Zone A.
   FLOOD INSURANCE RATE MAP (FIRM). An official map of a community, on which
the Federal Insurance Administration has delineated both the areas of special
flood hazards and the risk premium zones applicable to the community.
   FLOOD INSURANCE STUDY. The official report provided by the Federal Insurance
Administration. The report contains flood profiles, the water surface elevation
of the base flood, as well as the flood hazard boundary-floodway map.
   FLOODWAY. The channel of a river or other watercourse and the adjacent land
areas that must be reserved in order to discharge the base flood without
cumulatively increasing the water surface elevation more than one foot.
   HABITABLE FLOOR. Any floor usable for living purposes, which includes
working, sleeping, eating, cooking or recreation, or a combination thereof. A
floor used for storage purposes only is not a HABITABLE FLOOR.
   MEAN SEA LEVEL. The average height of the sea for all stages of the tide.
   MOBILE HOME. A structure, transportable in one or more sections, which is
built on permanent chassis and designed to be used with or without a permanent
foundation when connected to the required utilities. It does not include
recreational vehicles or travel trailers.
   NEW MOBILE HOME PARK OR MOBILE HOME SUBDIVISION. A parcel (or contiguous
parcels) of land divided into two or more mobile home lots for rent or sale for
which the construction of facilities for servicing the lot on which the mobile
home is to be affixed (including, at a minimum, the installation of utilities,
either final site grading or the pouring of concrete pads, and the construction
of streets) is completed on or after the original effective date of this
chapter.
   START OF CONSTRUCTION. The first placement of permanent construction of a
structure (other than a mobile home) on a site, such as the pouring of slabs or
footings or any work beyond the stage of excavation. Permanent construction
does not include land preparation, such as clearing, grading and filling; nor
does it include the installation of streets and/or walkways; nor does it
include excavation for a basement, footings, plots or foundations or the
erection of temporary forms; nor does it include the installation on the
property of accessory buildings, such as garages or sheds not occupied as
dwelling units, or not as part of the main structure. For a structure (other
than a mobile home) without a basement or poured footings, the START OF
CONSTRUCTION includes the first permanent framing or assembly of the structure
on any part thereof of its piling or foundation. For mobile homes not within a
mobile home park or mobile home subdivision, START OF CONSTRUCTION means the
affixing of the mobile home to its permanent site. For mobile homes within
mobile home parks or mobile home subdivisions, START OF CONSTRUCTION is the
date on which the construction of facilities for servicing the site on which
the mobile home is to be affixed (including, at a minimum, the construction of
streets, either final site grading or the pouring of concrete pads, and
installation of utilities) is completed.
   STRUCTURE. A walled and roofed building that is principally above ground, as
well as a mobile home.
   SUBSTANTIAL IMPROVEMENT.
      (1)   Any repair, reconstruction or improvement of a structure the cost
of which equals or exceeds 50% of the market value of the structure either:
         (a)   Before the improvement or repair is started; or
         (b)   If the structure has been damaged and is being restored, before
the damage occurred.
      (2)   For the purposes of this definition, SUBSTANTIAL IMPROVEMENT is
considered to occur when the first alteration of any wall, ceiling, floor or
other structural part of the building commences, whether or not that alteration
affects the external dimensions of the structure. The term does not, however,
include either:
         (a)   Any project for improvement of a structure to comply with
existing state or local health, sanitary or safety code specifications which
are solely necessary to assure safe living conditions; or
         (b)   Any alteration of a structure listed on the National Register of
Historic Places or a State Inventory of Historic Places.
   VARIANCE. A grant of relief to a person from the requirements of this
chapter when specific enforcement would result in unnecessary hardship. A
VARIANCE, therefore, permits construction or development in a manner otherwise
prohibited by the chapter.
(Prior Code, § 12-204)
§ 154.05 APPLICATION; COMPLIANCE; INTERPRETATION.
   (A)   This chapter shall apply to all areas of special flood hazard within
the jurisdiction of the town.
   (B)   No structure or land shall hereafter be located, altered or have its
use changed without full compliance with the terms of this chapter and other
applicable regulations.
   (C)   This chapter is not intended to repeat, abrogate or impair any
existing easements, covenants or deed restrictions. However, where this chapter
and another conflict or overlap, whichever imposes the more stringent
restrictions shall prevail.
   (D)   In the interpretation and application of this chapter, all provisions
shall be:
      (1)   Considered as minimum requirements;
      (2)   Liberally construed in favor of the governing body; and
      (3)   Deemed neither to limit nor repeal any other powers granted under
state statutes.
(Prior Code, § 12-205)
§ 154.06 BASIS FOR ESTABLISHING THE AREAS OF SPECIAL FLOOD HAZARD.
   The areas of special flood hazard identified by the Federal Insurance
Administration on its flood hazard boundary map (FHBM) for the town, and any
revisions thereto are hereby adopted by reference and declared to be a part of
this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 12-206)
§ 154.07 DEVELOPMENT PERMIT REQUIRED.
   A development permit shall be required to ensure conformance with the
provisions of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 12-207)
§ 154.08 WARNING AND DISCLAIMER OF LIABILITY.
   (A)   The degree of flood protection required by this chapter is considered
reasonable for regulatory purposes and is based on scientific and engineering
considerations. On rare occasions, greater floods can and will occur and flood
heights may be increased by human-made or natural causes.
   (B)   This chapter does not imply that land outside the areas of special
flood hazards or uses permitted within such areas will be free from flooding or
flood damages.
   (C)   This chapter shall not create liability on the part of the town or any
officer or employee thereof for any flood damages that result from reliance on
this chapter or any administrative decision lawfully made thereunder.
(Prior Code, § 12-208)
§ 154.09 DESIGNATION OF BUILDING INSPECTOR; DUTIES.
   (A)   The Town Building Inspector is hereby appointed to administer and
implement the provisions of this chapter.
   (B)   Duties and responsibilities of the Town Building Inspector shall
include, but not be limited to, the following:
      (1)   Maintain and hold open for public inspection all records pertaining
to the provisions of this chapter;
      (2)   Review, approve or deny all applications for development permits
required by §
154.07;
      (3)   Review permits for proposed development to assure that all
necessary permits have been obtained from those federal, state or local
governmental agencies from which prior approval is required;
      (4)   Make the necessary interpretation where interpretation is needed as
to the exact location of the boundaries of the areas of special flood hazards
(for example, where there appears to be conflict between a mapped boundary and
actual field conditions);
      (5)   Notify adjacent communities and the State Water Resources Board
prior to any alteration or relocation of a watercourse and submit evidence of
such notification to the Federal Insurance Administration;
      (6)   Assure that maintenance is provided within the altered or relocated
portion of the watercourse so that the flood-carrying capacity is not
diminished; and
      (7)   When base flood elevation data has not been provided in accordance
with §
154.06, obtain, review and reasonably utilize any base flood elevation data
available from a federal, state or other source, in order to administer the
provisions of §§
154.12 through
154.14.
(Prior Code, § 12-209)
§ 154.10 PERMIT PROCEDURES; APPROVAL OR DENIAL.
   (A)   Application for a development permit shall be presented to the Town
Building Inspector on forms furnished by him or her and may include, but not be
limited to, plans in duplicate drawn to scale showing the location, dimensions
and elevation of proposed landscape alterations, existing and proposed
structures, and the location of the foregoing in relation to areas of special
flood hazard. Additionally, the following information is required:
      (1)   Elevation, in relation to mean sea level, of the lowest floor
(including basement) of all proposed structures;
      (2)   Elevation, in relation to mean sea level, to which any
nonresidential structure shall be floodproofed;
      (3)   A certificate from a registered professional engineer or architect
that the nonresidential floodproofed structure shall meet the floodproofing
criteria of §
154.13; and
      (4)   Description of the extent to which any watercourse or natural
drainage will be altered or relocated us a result of proposed development.
   (B)   Approval or denial of a development permit by the Town Building
Inspector shall be based on all of the provisions of this chapter and the
following relevant factors:
      (1)   The danger to life and property due to flooding or erosion damage;
      (2)   The susceptibility of the proposed facility and its contents to
flood damage and the effect of such damage on the individual owner;
      (3)   The danger that materials may be swept onto other fonds to the
injury of others;
      (4)   The compatibility of the proposed use with existing and anticipated
development;
      (5)   The safety of access to the property in times of flood for ordinary
and emergency vehicles;
      (6)   The costs of providing governmental services during and after flood
conditions, including maintenance and repair of streets and bridges, and public
utilities and facilities such as sewer, gas, electrical and water systems;
      (7)   The expected heights, velocity, duration, rate of rise and sediment
transport of the floodwaters and the effects of wave action, if applicable,
expected at the site;
      (8)   The necessity to the facility of a waterfront location, where
applicable;
      (9)   The availability of alternative locations, not subject to flooding
or erosion damage, for the proposed use; and
      (10)   The relationship of the proposed use to the comprehensive plan for
that area.
(Prior Code, § 12-210)
§ 154.11 VARIANCE PROCEDURES.
   (A)   The Town Board of Trustees shall hear and render judgment on requests
for variances from the requirements of this chapter. It shall hear and render
judgment on an appeal only when it is alleged there is an error in any
requirement, decision or determination made by the Building Inspector in the
enforcement or administration of the chapter. Any person or persons aggrieved
by the decision of the Board of Adjustment may appeal such decision in the
courts of competent jurisdiction.
   (B)   Generally, variances may be issued for new construction and
substantial improvements to be erected on a lot of one-half acre or less in
size contiguous to and surrounded by lots with existing structures constructed
below the base flood level, providing the relevant factors in §
154.10(B) have been fully considered. As the lot size increases beyond one-half
acre, the technical justification required for issuing the variance increases.
Upon consideration of the factors noted above and the intent of this chapter,
the Board of Adjustment may attach such conditions to the granting of variances
as it deems necessary to further the purpose and objectives of §
154.01.
   (C)   Prerequisites for granting variances include the following:
      (1)   Variances shall only be issued upon a determination that the
variance is the minimum necessary, considering the flood hazard, to afford
relief;
      (2)   Variances shall only be issued upon:
         (a)   A showing of good and sufficient cause;
         (b)   A determination that failure to grant the variance would result
in exceptional hardship to the applicant; and
         (c)   A determination that the granting of a variance will not result
in increased flood heights, additional threats to public safety, extraordinary
public expense, create nuisances, cause fraud on or victimization of the public
or conflict with existing local laws or ordinances.
      (3)   Any applicant to whom a variance is granted shall be given written
notice that the structure will be permitted to be built with a lowest floor
elevation no more than two feet below the base flood elevation, and that the
cost of flood insurance will be commensurate with the increased risk resulting
from the reduced lowest floor elevation.
   (D)   Variances shall not be issued within any designated floodway if any
increase in flood levels during the base flood discharge would result.
   (E)   Variances may be issued for the reconstruction, rehabilitation or
restoration of structures listed on the National Register of Historic Places or
the State Inventory of Historic Places, without regard to the procedures set
forth in the remainder of this section.
   (F)   The Building Inspector shall maintain a record of all actions
involving an appeal and shall report variances to the Federal Insurance
Administration upon request.
(Prior Code, § 12-211)
§ 154.12 GENERAL STANDARDS; FLOOD HAZARD AREAS.
   In all areas of special flood hazards the following provisions are required:
   (A)   All new construction and substantial improvements shall be anchored to
prevent flotation, collapse or lateral movement of the structure;
   (B)   All new construction or substantial improvements shall be constructed
by methods and practices that minimize flood damage;
   (C)   All new construction or substantial improvements shall be constructed
with materials and utility equipment resistant to flood damage;
   (D)   All new and replacement water supply systems shall be designed to
minimize or eliminate infiltration of floodwaters into the system;
   (E)   New and replacement sanitary sewage systems shall be designed to
minimize or eliminate infiltration of floodwaters into the system and
discharges from the systems into floodwaters; and
   (F)   On-site waste disposal systems shall be located to avoid impairment to
them or contamination from them during flooding.
(Prior Code, § 12-212)
§ 154.13 SPECIFIC STANDARDS; FLOOD HAZARD AREAS.
   In all areas of special flood hazards where base flood elevation data has
been provided as set forth in §§
154.06,
154.09 and
154.14, the following provisions are required.
   (A)   Residential construction. New construction or substantial improvement
of any residential structure shall have the lowest floor, including basement,
elevated to or above the base flood elevation. A registered professional
engineer, architect or land surveyor shall submit a certification to the Town
Engineer that the standard of this division (A), as proposed in §
154.10 is satisfied.
   (B)   Nonresidential construction.
      (1)   New construction or substantial improvement of any commercial,
industrial or other nonresidential structure shall either have the lowest
floor, including basement, elevated to the level of the base flood elevation
or, together with attendant utility and sanitary facilities, be floodproofed so
that below the base flood level the structure is watertight with walls
substantially impermeable to the passage of water and with structural
components having the capability of resisting hydrostatic and hydrodynamic
loads and effects of buoyancy.
      (2)   A registered professional engineer or architect shall submit a
certification to the Town Engineer that the standards of this paragraph as
proposed in §
154.10 are satisfied.
   (C)   Mobile homes. No mobile home shall be placed in a floodway or, if
applicable, a coastal high hazard area, except in an existing mobile home park
or existing mobile home subdivision. All mobile homes shall be anchored to
resist flotation, collapse or lateral movement. Specific requirements shall be:
      (1)   Over-the-top ties at each of the four corners of the mobile home,
with two additional ties per side at intermediate locations and mobile homes
less than 50 feet long requiring one additional tie per side;
      (2)   Frame ties at each corner of the home with five additional ties per
side at intermediate points and mobile homes less than 50 feet long requiring
four additional ties per side;
      (3)   All components of the anchoring system be capable of carrying a
force of 4,800 pounds; and
      (4)   Any additions to the mobile home be similarly anchored.
(Prior Code, § 12-213)
§ 154.14 STANDARDS FOR SUBDIVISION PROPOSALS; FLOOD HAZARD AREAS.
   (A)   All subdivision proposals shall be consistent with §§
154.01 through
154.03.
   (B)   All proposals for the development of subdivisions shall meet
development permit requirements of §§
154.07,
154.10 and
154.12 through
154.14.
   (C)   Base flood elevation data shall be generated for subdivision proposals
and other proposed development which is greater than the lesser of 50 lots or
five acres, if not otherwise provided pursuant to §§
154.06 and
154.09.
   (D)   All subdivision proposals shall have adequate drainage provided to
reduce exposure to flood hazards.
   (E)   All subdivision proposals shall have public utilities and facilities
such as sewer, gas, electrical and water systems located and constructed to
minimize flood damage.
(Prior Code, § 12-214)
CHAPTER 155: PLANNING AND DEVELOPMENT
Section
   
155.01   More than one dwelling per lot prohibited
   
155.02   Temporary exception application
   
155.03   Requirements of exceptions
 
   
155.99   Penalty
§ 155.01 MORE THAN ONE DWELLING PER LOT PROHIBITED.
   No person or other entity may establish more than one single dwelling per
one platted lot within the town limits of the town.
(Prior Code, § 12-101)
§ 155.02 TEMPORARY EXCEPTION APPLICATION.
   A temporary exception to this chapter may be requested of the Town Board of
Trustees by petitioning the Board of Trustees requesting that another dwelling
be placed on the platted lot.
(Prior Code, § 12-102)
§ 155.03 REQUIREMENTS OF EXCEPTIONS.
   Such temporary exception to this chapter, as provided in §
155.02, may be granted if sufficient proof of need is furnished to the Board of
Trustees. Any such temporary exception so granted shall not exceed a period of
12 months from the date thereof. Such exception shall be automatically revoked
upon its expiration date unless the Board of Trustees is requested to review
the exception and upon such review shall renew such exception for an additional
period not to exceed 12 months. Automatic revocation shall occur on each
subsequent expiration date thereafter subject to the same annual review with
additional maximum periods of 12 months extensions to be authorized only upon
review by the Board of Trustees. A signed affidavit is required stating the
need for this second dwelling and that no fee (e.g., rent) be imposed for the
use of the second dwelling, with a signed affidavit to be required upon each
subsequent request for extension, the affidavit to state that the facts and
conditions of the matter remain the same as set forth in the original
application.
(Prior Code, § 12-103)
§ 155.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person or entity who violates the provisions of this chapter shall
be notified to abate such violation within ten days. Failure to abate shall
constitute a misdemeanor and upon conviction is punishable as provided in §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 12-104)
   (B)   In addition to proceeding under authority of division (A) above, the
town is entitled to pursue all other civil remedies to which it is entitled in
order to enjoin a violation hereof against a person or entity so violating
same.
(Prior Code, § 12-105)
CHAPTER 156: ZONING CODE
Section
   
156.01   Title
   
156.02   Purpose
   
156.03   Definitions
   
156.04   Establishment of zoning districts
   
156.05   Zoning map
   
156.06   Use regulations
   
156.07   Development standards
   
156.08   Administration and enforcement
   
156.09   Amendments
 
   
156.99   Penalty
§ 156.01 TITLE.
   This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the Kellyville Zoning Code.
(Ord. 2024-002, passed 7-9-2024)
§ 156.02 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of this chapter is to promote the health, safety, morals and
general welfare of the community by establishing comprehensive zoning
regulations governing the use and development of land within the town.
(Ord. 2024-002, passed 7-9-2024)
§ 156.03 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   AGRICULTURAL DISTRICT (A). Areas designated for farming and agricultural
use.
   COMMERCIAL DISTRICT (C). Areas designated for businesses and commercial
activities.
   INDUSTRIAL DISTRICT (I). Areas designated for manufacturing, processing and
other industrial activities.
   RESIDENTIAL DISTRICT (R). Areas designated primarily for single-family and
multi-family dwellings.
   ZONING DISTRICT. A designated section of the town for which specific land
use regulations are prescribed.
(Ord. 2024-002, passed 7-9-2024)
§ 156.04 ESTABLISHMENT OF ZONING DISTRICTS.
   The town is hereby divided into the following zoning districts:
   (A)   Residential District (R);
   (B)   Commercial District (C);
   (C)   Industrial District (I); and
   (D)   Agricultural District (A).
(Ord. 2024-002, passed 7-9-2024)
§ 156.05 ZONING MAP.
   The boundaries of the zoning districts are shown on the official zoning map
of the town, which is hereby adopted and made a part of this chapter. The
zoning map shall be maintained in the office of the Town Clerk and shall be
available for public inspection.
(Ord. 2024-002, passed 7-9-2024)
§ 156.06 USE REGULATIONS.
   (A)   Residential District (R). 
      (1)   Permitted uses.
         (a)   Single-family dwellings;
         (b)   Multi-family dwellings; and
         (c)   Parks and recreational facilities.
      (2)   Conditional uses. 
         (a)   Home-based businesses; and
         (b)   Schools and educational institutions.
   (B)   Commercial District (C).
      (1)   Permitted uses.
         (a)   Retail stores;
         (b)   Restaurants; and
         (c)   Offices.
      (2)   Conditional uses.
         (a)   Hotels and motels; and
         (b)   Entertainment venues.
   (C)   Industrial District (I). 
      (1)   Permitted uses.
         (a)   Manufacturing plants;
         (b)   Warehouses; and
         (c)   Distribution centers.
      (2)   Conditional uses. 
         (a)   Heavy industrial activities; and
         (b)   Research and development facilities.
   (D)   Agricultural District (A). 
      (1)   Permitted uses.
         (a)   Crop production;
         (b)   Livestock farming; and
         (c)   Nurseries.
      (2)   Conditional uses.
         (a)   Agricultural processing facilities; and
         (b)   Farm-based tourism.
(Ord. 2024-002, passed 7-9-2024)
§ 156.07 DEVELOPMENT STANDARDS.
   (A)   Residential District (R). 
      (1)   Minimum lot size: 3,750 feet;
      (2)   Minimum living size: 1,000 square feet;
      (3)   Maximum building height: 26 feet; and
      (4)   Setback requirements: 25 feet front, 15 feet rear and ten feet
side.
   (B)   Commercial District (C). 
      (1)   Minimum lot size: 5,000 feet;
      (2)   Maximum building height: 35 feet; and
      (3)   Setback requirements: 25 feet front, 15 feet rear and ten feet
side.
   (C)   Industrial District (I).
      (1)   Minimum lot size: two acres;
      (2)   Maximum building height: 45 feet; and
      (3)   Setback requirements: 75 feet front, 50 feet rear and 75 feet side.
   (D)   Agricultural District (A). 
      (1)   Minimum lot size: two acres;
      (2)   Maximum building height: 35 feet; and
      (3)   Setback requirements: 25 feet front, 15 feet rear and ten feet
side.
(Ord. 2024-002, passed 7-9-2024)
§ 156.08 ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT.
   (A)   The administration and enforcement of this chapter shall be the
responsibility of the Town Administrator, who shall be appointed by the Town
Board.
   (B)   No building or structure shall be erected, moved, added to or
structurally altered without a permit issued by the Town Clerk.
(Ord. 2024-002, passed 7-9-2024) Penalty, see §
156.99
§ 156.09 AMENDMENTS.
   This chapter may be amended by the Town Board upon recommendation of the
Town Administrator, following a public hearing.
(Ord. 2024-002, passed 7-9-2024)
§ 156.99 PENALTY.
   Any person, firm or corporation violating any provision of this chapter
shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be fined not more
than $280 for each offense. Each day that a violation continues shall
constitute a separate offense.
(Ord. 2024-002, passed 7-9-2024)
